They also enthusiastically handled all the insurance hassles, the rental car situation, and kept in touch with me often to let me know how it was going.  I have had at least two other cars and and a pick up truck repaired at their facility and I must say, I couldn't possibly ask for better service or better results.

It turns out that everyone is enthusiastic, respectful, friendly, yet professional.

Getting in a car accident is never fun, but the attitudes of the folks at G & C make it a pleasure.

It is a treat to do business with these wonderful people.< /text><username>Bill Leeman< /username>< resp>

< text>
Classics Auto Body deserves a 10 STAR RATING. The shop did a beautiful job repairing a minor fender bender & repainting my entire classic 1985 Afla Romeo Spider.  This was the first accident for my car and I'm the original owner. So I was obsessed with the fact that any repair work done would not match the present condition of my paint job which admittedly had begun to dull.  However, I learned that the other driver's insurance company would not pay for a full repaint of the car & would only cover repair work, repainting of damage & a blend to adjacent panels. I researched several highly recommended restoration shops in the LA area & none of them thought the insurance company would pay the lion's share.

My insurance agent @ Farmers recommended I speak with Michael Krem, the owner of Classics Auto Body, a preferred Farmers Shop.  I realized immediately Michael was a straight shooter who would be a strong advocate for me in negotiating with the other party's insurance company.  Turns out he was fantastic!!! Michael negotiated a substantial increase over what other shops suggested I would get.

Classics repair crew & estimator Miguel were outstanding.  Michael gave me weekly updates & texted constant photos of my car‚Äôs progress.  They did additional work not included in their quote at no additional charge to maintain the quality of my car‚Äôs restoration.  Michael coordinated with my Alfa repair shop for any parts that needed sourcing & replacement.  He even coordinated taking my car to a convertible top shop that provided a discount for a new top (not part of the original plan but something I thought was essential once I realized the top would not match my shiny new car).

They delivered on time and not a penny more from their original estimate.  The quote they provided for entirely repainting my car was very competitive to the other shops' estimates.  The final color match was perfect.

This process was a dream come true when I was worried about my worst nightmare trying to restore my car to it‚Äôs original condition.  Let‚Äôs not forget this occurred during the peak of COVID lockdown.  No detail was left unattended. When I finally picked up the car, about 1 mile from the shop, a driver pulled up next to me at a stop light, rolled down his window and asked what year was my car, remarking that it was in MINT CONDITION.  I almost wondered if Michael hired someone to follow me and make this observation.  You can‚Äôt make this stuff up!

In conclusion, I highly recommend Classics Auto Body for any repair or body work related to classic cars, custom high end vehicles & ordinary cars based upon my experience.  This is a first class operation run by an owner who takes great pride in the final product.< /text>

I grew up on Balboa Island and, now that I live in New York City, I make sure to get my kids down to the Island for a trip across the bay on the ferry every time that we visit (usually twice a year). We get on the ferry on the Island, walk through the fun zone (stopping here and there for an arcade game with the girls), then to the Balboa Peninsula and it the Pacific for a dip and--if the waves allow--a bit of bodysurfing! What a blast!!!</Review>

<Text>OC is known for beautiful beach fronts and  Newport is one of the best spots for a nice cool breeze by a short amusing ferry trip! You will be hopping from the island side (it is called 'Balboa island') to the Peninsula for about 5 to 7 min. ride on a small fleet that can carry up to 3 mid sized cars and 20 to 30 people at a time. It only costs a buck or two per person and a little more for an automobile. On the Peninsula side, there are things to ride as you may see from a small village festival such as wheel ride and also many restuarants for pizza or burgers.< /Text>< Time>

I might be a little late to the ferry party, but I've never been to Balboa Island. After taking a trip down there, I found out why: Balboa Island is like a really small Seal Beach with no parking.

I came in over the bridge and left on the ferry. There were signs everywhere. If you can't find it, you're one of those people. I paid $2 for the car and I. It was weird, but I guess on an off day with no line it would be more convenient than driving around.

Low profile cars need to take it slow. The ramp is really steep and I was afraid of scraping my front end.<//Text>
